eye.”","66d5c3d1d0ec1aefc7d7219e","IoT Research","iot-research","whitepapers",false,"66d5c3d1d0ec1aefc7d721a1","66d5c3d1d0ec1aefc7d721a2","all","All",2,"Free Tools","yearly","noreply@blogapp.bitdefender.com",1,"product-updates","Product Updates","66d5c3d2d0ec1aefc7d722d2","60 Hurts per Second – How We Got Access to Enough Solar Power to Run the United States","60-hurts-per-second-how-we-got-access-to-enough-solar-power-to-run-the-united-states","https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F08\u002F1ZZ96uESRJQ.jpg","2024-08-07T16:16:00.000+03:00","\u003Cp\u003EThe electricity grid – the buzzing, crackling marvel that supplies the lifeblood of modernity - is by far the largest structure humanity ever built. It’s so big, in fact, that few people even notice it, like a fish can’t see the ocean.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EUntil the grid goes down, that is. Then, like the fish dangling from the angler’s hook, we see our vulnerability. Modernity dissolves into a sudden silence, followed by the repeated flick of a light switch, and a howl of panic at the prospect of missed appointments, ruined dinners, lost workdays, stopped elevators and dark, cold evenings, and worse.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBut most of the time, the grid hums along just fine ...\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ENow, take that labyrinthine system and add another complex network, this one delivering hundreds of gigawatts of power from the sun - solar power infrastructure. This ever-fluctuating source of energy is tapped via rooftop panels, distant solar farms, slapdash home arrays and other evolving infrastructure around the globe.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAnd with complexity comes risk ...\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThen, take those two systems and intersect them with the Internet of Things, an ethereal network that runs from the limits of human thought – both positive and malicious – into the routines of daily life through seemingly innocuous gadgets.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAt that intersection we find the mundane world of inverters and controllers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAnd that's where a group of researchers stumbled upon an alarming fact:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003Ea solar grid responsible for 195 gigawatts, or 20 percent of the world’s solar power output, is vulnerable. That’s enough to power the entire United States - and it’s just waiting to be hijacked.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"key-findings\"\u003EKey Findings\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EBitdefender researchers have identified a series of vulnerabilities in PV plant management platforms operated by Solarman and Deye.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThis platform is responsible for coordinating production operations of millions of solar installations worldwide generating a whopping output of approximately 195 GW of solar power (20% of the global solar production)\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EIf exploited, these vulnerabilities could allow an attacker to control inverter settings that could take parts of the grid down, potentially causing blackouts.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThese vulnerabilities have been communicated to the affected vendors and fixed.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"understanding-the-power-grid\"\u003EUnderstanding the Power Grid\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe power grid is a vast network of power plants, transmission lines and distribution systems that delivers electricity from producers to consumers. It consists of three main components:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Col\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EGeneration\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: Power plants generate electricity using various sources, including coal, natural gas, nuclear, hydro and, increasingly, solar and wind.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ETransmission\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: High-voltage transmission lines carry electricity over long distances from power plants to substations.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EDistribution\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: Substations lower the voltage for safe distribution to homes and businesses through local power lines.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Fol\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe grid balances supply and demand in real time, ensuring that electricity is available when needed. When generation exceeds demand, voltage in the grid rises to dangerous levels that can damage sensitive equipment connected to it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhen generation can't meet demand, anomalies begin to occur. Initially, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Farstechnica.com\u002Ftech-policy\u002F2018\u002F03\u002Fovens-across-europe-display-the-wrong-time-due-to-a-serbia-kosovo-grid-dispute\u002F?ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003Eyour microwave oven may get several minutes slower\u003C\u002Fa\u003E (as it computes its current time based on the “ticks” in the network measured in Hertz: 60 Hertz - or cycles per second - in the US, and 50 Hz in Europe). Secondly, parts of the grid where the imbalance is detected are disconnected before they drag the whole system into a downwards spiral that can take days to recover from.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F08\u002Fimage.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"904\" height=\"500\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F08\u002Fimage.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F08\u002Fimage.png 904w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EFascinated? To learn more about how the grid works, you might want to watch \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=v1BMWczn7JM&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003Ethis episode of Practical Engineering\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"the-role-of-solar-energy-in-the-grid\"\u003EThe Role of Solar Energy in the Grid\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESolar energy has a powerful impact on the energy landscape. Solar panels convert sunlight into a clean, renewable source of power, which can be used immediately, stored in batteries, or fed into the grid.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESolar power systems are often decentralized, meaning they are installed on individual homes or businesses rather than centralized power plants. This means that generation and distribution often take place in the same ZIP code and (with some exceptions such as solar power production in parks), disruptions at this level have a limited geographic impact.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis decentralization presents several challenges and opportunities for the grid. Solar power reduces dependence on fossil fuels, lowers greenhouse gas emissions, and can enhance grid resilience by distributing power generation. However, integrating numerous small-scale solar systems into the grid can complicate management.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESolar setups produce variable amounts of electricity, and only during daytime.  Maintaining voltage levels and managing the variability of solar power must  be outsourced to a pre-programmed critical component called an inverter. An inverter converts the direct current (DC) electricity generated by solar panels into alternating current (AC) electricity, the standard used by most homes and businesses, as well as for transmission over the power grid.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe inverter performs two primary functions in a solar power system:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EDC to AC Conversion\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: Solar panels generate DC electricity  however, most electrical appliances and the power grid operate on AC electricity, which alternates in polarity and voltage. The inverter converts the DC electricity into AC electricity to  be used by household appliances or fed into the grid.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EGrid Synchronization\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: In grid-tied solar power systems, the inverter  synchronizes the phase and frequency of the AC output with the grid. This ensures that the electricity generated by the solar panels is compatible with the grid and can be safely exported to it. Differences in phase and voltage can crash the grid.  Power distributors and governments  see any deliberate attempts to bypass these grid safety measures as a threat to national security.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"security-flaws-in-solar-management-platforms\"\u003ESecurity Flaws in Solar Management Platforms\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBitdefender researchers  started looking into potential cybercriminal use of  inverters, as they are becoming increasingly visible on the radar of internet-connected devices. By the foresight of “we had one already available and we wanted to test it,” we  looked into data loggers made by Solarman that are a popular choice for monitoring Deye inverter units..\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ETo add context, Solarman is one of the world’s largest photovoltaic (PV) monitoring and management platform, and equipment connected to this platform is apparently responsible for the production of over \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.solarmanpv.com\u002Fcorporate\u002Fabout-us\u002F?ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003E195 gigawatts of power across 2M+ active PV plants involving \"10M+ devices in 190+ countries and territories”.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EA quick look at the platform shows Solarman is not only an equipment builder,  they also license parts of their infrastructure to other manufacturers (see the Appendix). Our analysis shows that the Solarman API architecture has multiple entry points exposed for multiple companies selling inverters, data loggers and a wide range of PV equipment. The investigation of the Deye inverter and Solarman data logger have uncovered severe security vulnerabilities that could be exploited to disrupt or even take down the grid.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003ENote - a data logger in an inverter setup records and transmits data on the solar power system's performance. It enables real-time and historical monitoring, fault detection, and remote management, ensuring the system operates efficiently and reliably. By gathering metrics such as power output, voltage and current, the data logger helps optimize energy production and usage, facilitates maintenance through timely alerts, and integrates with cloud platforms for accessible remote monitoring. This management feature improves system performance, enhances reliability, and supports informed decision-making, ultimately contributing to the longevity and effectiveness of the solar power installation.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe Solarman platform is linked to a variety of equipment and brands revolving around it. Many of these customers seem to use the entire platform as a service, while others wrap API endpoints in custom implementations and keep customer databases private.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBeyond the multiple entry-points exposed by the platform (discussed above), we sought to discover how various parts of this architecture fit together. To validate our assumptions, we successfully attempted to register a Solarman data logger into the Deye platform.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAs far as we are able to tell, Deye has been using the original Solarman infrastructure up until 2024, but they \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.deyeinverter.com\u002Fnews\u002Fcompany-news\u002Fdeye-cloud-account-transfer.html?ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003Ehave customized their implementation\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and spun off a new datacenter to accommodate their own user base.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe Solarman platform has two types of accounts: one is regular reporting, where the logged-in user has access to production and usage data in real time, while the other is a business (contractor) account used by the authorized installation company to control devices, modify voltage or frequency and control other power grid injection settings). With these details out of the way, it’s time to dig into how we managed to gain access to all business and regular accounts in all solar production devices made by Solarman and its partners.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"vulnerabilities-in-the-solarman-platform\"\u003EVulnerabilities in the Solarman platform\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EOur research on the Solarman platform uncovered the following vulnerabilities: (These flaws are detailed in a separate paper available below.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n        \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-card kg-file-card kg-file-card-medium\"\u003E\n            \u003Ca class=\"kg-file-card-container\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Ffiles\u002F2024\u002F08\u002FBitdefender-PReport-solarman-creat7907.pdf\" title=\"Download\" download\u003E\n                \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-contents\"\u003E\n                    \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-title\"\u003EVulnerabilities in the Solarman platform\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                    \n                    \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-metadata\"\u003E\n                        \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-filename\"\u003EBitdefender-PReport-solarman-creat7907.pdf\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                        \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-filesize\"\u003E974 KB\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                    \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-icon\"\u003E\n                    \u003Csvg xmlns=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.w3.org\u002F2000\u002Fsvg\" viewBox=\"0 0 24 24\"\u003E\u003Cdefs\u003E\u003Cstyle\u003E.a{fill:none;stroke:currentColor;stroke-linecap:round;stroke-linejoin:round;stroke-width:1.5px;}\u003C\u002Fstyle\u003E\u003C\u002Fdefs\u003E\u003Ctitle\u003Edownload-circle\u003C\u002Ftitle\u003E\u003Cpolyline class=\"a\" points=\"8.25 14.25 12 18 15.75 14.25\"\u002F\u003E\u003Cline class=\"a\" x1=\"12\" y1=\"6.75\" x2=\"12\" y2=\"18\"\u002F\u003E\u003Ccircle class=\"a\" cx=\"12\" cy=\"12\" r=\"11.25\"\u002F\u003E\u003C\u002Fsvg\u003E\n                \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n            \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\n        \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n        \u003Col\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EFull Account Takeover\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: The Solarman platform’s \u003Ccode\u003E\u002Foauth2-s\u002Foauth\u002Ftoken\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E API endpoint lets attackers generate authorization tokens for any account. By modifying the JSON payload, attackers can gain control over any regular or business account. This means that a malicious user could iterate through all accounts, take over any of them and modify inverter parameters or change the way the inverter interacts with the grid.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EToken Reuse Across Platforms\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: JWT tokens issued by the Deye Cloud platform are also valid on the Solarman platform, granting full access to the accounts based on their ID. This cross-platform vulnerability can lead to widespread unauthorized access in the absence of well-defined boundaries to isolate vendors.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EExcessive Data Exposure\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: The Solarman platform’s API endpoints return excessive information about organizations, including private details such as email addresses and phone numbers. This information can be harvested to exploit the platform’s users and organizations. In addition to personally identifiable information, an attacker can chain this with the first vulnerability to run subsequent queries on the account and obtain GPS coordinates for solar installations as well as their real-time production capacity.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Fol\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"vulnerabilities-in-the-deye-platform\"\u003EVulnerabilities in the Deye platform\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Col\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EHard-Coded Credentials\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: The Deye platform uses a hard-coded account (`SmartConfigurator@solarmanpv.com` with password \u003Ccode\u003E123456\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E) to access device data. This account can obtain an authorization token that grants access to any device, exposing sensitive information such as software versions, Wi-Fi credentials, and more​ (see the Deye disclosure report available below)​.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EInformation Leakage\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: The API endpoint \u003Ccode\u003E\u002Fuser-s\u002Facc\u002Forgs\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E on eu1.deyecloud.com returns excessive private information about users, including names, email addresses, phone numbers and user IDs. This endpoint can be exploited to leak information about all users on the platform​.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EAuthorization Token Generation\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: The \u003Ccode\u003E\u002Foauth-s\u002Foauth\u002F\u003C\u002Fcode\u003Etoken API endpoint has the same vulnerability as the endpoint used by Solarman. However, the JWT token that is generated contains a wrong value and is not accepted by the server, even though the token is valid and signed. This issue could pose a future risk if not properly patched​.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Fol\u003E\n        \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-card kg-file-card kg-file-card-medium\"\u003E\n            \u003Ca class=\"kg-file-card-container\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Ffiles\u002F2024\u002F08\u002FBitdefender-PReport-deye-creat7907.pdf\" title=\"Download\" download\u003E\n                \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-contents\"\u003E\n                    \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-title\"\u003EVulnerabilities in the Deye platform\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                    \n                    \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-metadata\"\u003E\n                        \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-filename\"\u003EBitdefender-PReport-deye-creat7907.pdf\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                        \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-filesize\"\u003E2 MB\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                    \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-icon\"\u003E\n                    \u003Csvg xmlns=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.w3.org\u002F2000\u002Fsvg\" viewBox=\"0 0 24 24\"\u003E\u003Cdefs\u003E\u003Cstyle\u003E.a{fill:none;stroke:currentColor;stroke-linecap:round;stroke-linejoin:round;stroke-width:1.5px;}\u003C\u002Fstyle\u003E\u003C\u002Fdefs\u003E\u003Ctitle\u003Edownload-circle\u003C\u002Ftitle\u003E\u003Cpolyline class=\"a\" points=\"8.25 14.25 12 18 15.75 14.25\"\u002F\u003E\u003Cline class=\"a\" x1=\"12\" y1=\"6.75\" x2=\"12\" y2=\"18\"\u002F\u003E\u003Ccircle class=\"a\" cx=\"12\" cy=\"12\" r=\"11.25\"\u002F\u003E\u003C\u002Fsvg\u003E\n                \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n            \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\n        \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n        \u003Ch2 id=\"implications-for-grid-security\"\u003EImplications for Grid Security\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhile most of our previous findings have a serious impact on the individual or on the internet itself, the flaws detailed in this research are fundamentally different. Access to devices interacting with the grid can have devastating effects on the proper functioning of the grid itself. These vulnerabilities pose a significant threat to grid security in several ways:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EUnauthorized Control\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: Attackers can take over accounts and control solar inverters, disrupting power generation and potentially causing voltage fluctuations.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EData Breaches\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: Sensitive information about users and organizations can be leaked, leading to privacy violations, information harvesting, targeted phishing attacks or other malicious activities.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EOperational Disruptions\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: By accessing and modifying settings on solar inverters, attackers can cause widespread disruptions in power distribution, impacting grid stability and potentially leading to blackouts.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"disclosure-timeline\"\u003EDisclosure Timeline\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"solarman\"\u003ESolarman:\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMay 22, 2024: Bitdefender reaches out to Solarman for a security contact\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMay 23, 2024: Bitdefender gets in touch with Solarman security team and sends vulnerability information\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMay 24, 2024: Vulnerabilities acknowledged; account takeover gets immediately fixed\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJun 17, 2024: Vendor confirms that a fix for the API returning too much information is in place.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJul 17, 2024: Vendor confirms that the Deye token reuse issue is now fixed.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"deye\"\u003EDeye:\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMay 22, 2024: Bitdefender reaches out to Deye for a security contact\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJun 03, 2024: Authorized security partner asks Bitdefender for details\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJun 06, 2024: Bitdefender sends the vulnerability report\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJun 17, 2024: Bitdefender asks for an update on the reported issues\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJul 09, 2024: Deye sends an overview of the fixed issues\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EAug 07, 2024: This report becomes public as per the coordinated vulnerability disclosure protocols.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"conclusion\"\u003EConclusion\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIntegrating solar power into the grid offers immense benefits, but it also introduces attack surfaces that equipment makers must take into account. The security flaws found in the Deye and Solarman platforms highlight the need for robust cybersecurity in managing solar energy systems, as well as in general IoT setups.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EProtecting the grid from cyber threats is crucial to ensuring reliable and secure power for all. As we continue to embrace renewable energy, we must also remain vigilant and proactive in securing our energy infrastructure against evolving threats.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe’d like to thank the vendors involved for acknowledging and fixing these vulnerabilities in a timely manner.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EToo long for a read? Watch this piece of research as a video presentation on August 9 at 5\u003C\u002Fem\u003E:00PM (Creator Stage 2\u003Cem\u003E @ the IoT Village talks) at Defcon. If you are attending Defcon 32 in person, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.iotvillage.org\u002Fdefcon.html?ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003Ecome see the talk live\u003C\u002Fa\u003E or meet and greet the researchers.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"appendix\"\u003EAppendix\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHere is a list of Solarman partner companies using the platform and potentially affected by the reported vulnerabilities. Our testing reveals that most of these vendors have scheduled maintentance windows to deploy security patches. We presume that these scheduled maintenance intervals are set to implement mitigations for the issues we reported to Solarman and Deye.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-begin: Smart TVs and streaming devices account for a whopping 20% [pdf] of all connected IoT devices, and potential vulnerabilities in firmware could affect a significant user base.\n\nAs","\u002Fblog\u002Flabs\u002Fvulnerabilities-identified-amazon-fire-tv-stick-insignia-fire-os-tv-series\u002F","66d5c3d2d0ec1aefc7d722b5","EyeSpy - Iranian Spyware Delivered in VPN Installers","eyespy-iranian-spyware-delivered-in-vpn-installers","https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2023\u002F01\u002Feyespy-1.jpg","2023-01-11T13:00:00.000+03:00","Consumer VPN solutions have witnessed explosive growth in the past few years. These ubiquitous utilities help users keep their internet traffic private, surf anonymously, and bypass restrictions or censorship. And, while most of the world takes this technology for granted,  users in specific regions - such as the people in Iran - have to try out dozens of apps before they find one that is (still) able to bypass ISP restrictions. And, while some VPNs are fake [here is a guide on how to spot a fak","\u002Fblog\u002Flabs\u002Feyespy-iranian-spyware-delivered-in-vpn-installers\u002F","66d5c3d2d0ec1aefc7d722d0","Unfading Sea Haze: New Espionage Campaign in the South China Sea","unfading-sea-haze-new-espionage-campaign-in-the-south-china-sea","https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F05\u002Fdiver-1850255_1920.jpg","2024-05-22T17:45:00.000+03:00","\u003Cp\u003EBitdefender researchers investigated a series of incidents at high-level organizations in countries of the South China Sea region, all performed by the same  threat actor we track as Unfading Sea Haze. Based on the victimology and the cyber-attack’s aim, we believe the threat actor is aligned with China’s interests.\u003Cbr\u003EAs tensions in the region rise, they are reflected in the intensification of activity on behalf of the Unfading Sea Haze actor, which uses new and improved tools and TTPs.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe noticed multiple times that the actor was regaining access to the victim’s systems either because of improper credential hygiene or because of bad patching strategies of the edge devices and exposed web services. Thus, this publication intends to raise awareness of the importance of respecting essential best practices that ensure security and to share with the community information that could help detect and disrupt Unfading Sea Haze’s espionage activities.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"key-findings\"\u003EKey findings\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe Unfading Sea Haze impacted at least 8 military and government organizations, a threat actor that has been active at least since 2018.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EOne of the infection vectors used by Unfading Sea Haze is spear phishing with zip archives containing lnk deploying SerialPktdoor backdoor.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe tools of choice for Unfading Sea Haze’s post-compromise activity are .net payloads sharpJsHandler and SerialPktDoor and two variations of the Gh0stRat—EtherealGh0st and FluffyGh0st—which evolved from two other old variants, TranslucentGh0st and SilentGh0st, used by the threat actor since at least 2018.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe actor uses the legitimate RMM, presumably as a backup access point into the victim’s network.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe aim of the activity is espionage, the actor presenting an interest in doc, docx, pdf, txt, and ppt files, also targeting browser data and cookies, and exfiltrating Telegram, Viber, and other messaging app files\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003EA full analysis of the attack is available in the whitepaper below:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-begin: html--\u003E\u003Cp Based on the victimology and the cyber-attack’s aim, we believe the threat actor is aligned with China’s interests.\nAs tensions in the region rise, they are reflected in the intensification of activity on behalf of the Unfading Sea Haze actor, which uses new and improved tools and TTPs.\n\nWe notice","\u002Fblog\u002Flabs\u002Funfading-sea-haze-new-espionage-campaign-in-the-south-china-sea\u002F","66d5c3d2d0ec1aefc7d722cd","AI meets next-gen info stealers in social media malvertising campaigns","ai-meets-next-gen-info-stealers-in-social-media-malvertising-campaigns","https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002Fmalvertising-campaigns-Bitdefender-Labs.jpg","2024-04-04T16:00:00.000+03:00","\u003Cp\u003EThe impact that AI has on society has steadily crept into the darkest nooks and crannies of the internet. So much so that cybercrooks are hitching free rides on the AI bandwagon by leveraging the increased demand of AI-powered software for content creators.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ECybercriminal groups constantly adapt their operating methods and tools to stay a step ahead of potential victims. Highly focused on enhancing their deceptive practices, threat actors have, unfortunately, found a most reliable and powerful ally in artificial intelligence.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBitdefender researchers are keeping a close eye on these deceptive efforts and exploits regarding the rising popularity of generative artificial intelligence software to keep consumers aware and help protect their devices, data and money.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EOver the past year, Bitdefender Labs has seen a motley crew of AI-powered illicit operations conducted by threat actors over social media, from stream-jacking attacks that delivered crypto-doubling schemes on YouTube to audio deep fakes that overflow on Meta’s social platforms.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis paper focuses on nefarious activities that take advantage of the demand and supply of some of the most popular generative AI software to attack users from across the globe.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"key-findings\"\u003EKey findings:\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003ECybercrooks have taken over Facebook profiles to run sponsored malvertising campaigns impersonating Midjourney, Sora AI, DALL-E 3, Evoto, ChatGPT 5 and many others\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe malicious pages on Facebook are meticulously designed to trick users into downloading purportedly official desktop versions of popular AI software. The cybercriminals behind these campaigns regularly change and adapt the malicious payloads in an attempt to avoid further detection from security software\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe links direct users to malicious webpages that download a variety of intrusive stealers to harvest sensitive information from compromised systems, including credentials, autocomplete data, credit card information, and even crypto wallet information.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe analyzed campaigns employ malicious ads that contain links to executable files that serve Rilide, Vidar, IceRAT, Nova Stealers. The entire batch of malicious software is often offered as malware-as-a-service by threat actors on specialized forums and channels.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe malvertising campaigns have tremendous reach through Meta’s sponsored ad system and have actively been targeting European users from Germany, Poland, Italy, France, Belgium, Spain, the Netherlands, Romania, Sweden, and elsewhere.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe ads use convincing descriptions alongside generated AI videos and photos to lure potential users into accessing malicious payloads\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EOne particular Facebook page impersonating Midjourney with a whopping 1.2 million followers was active for nearly a year until it was shut down on March 8, 2024. Since then threat actors have continuously set up more fraudulent pages to deliver malicious ads to users.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe Midjourney malvertising ad campaign was directed towards male Facebook users aged 25 to 55 and had an ad reach of approximately 500,000 individuals from Europe (demographics and reach of the campaign were obtained by tracking Meta’s Ad Library catalog)\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"organizing-the-attacks\"\u003EOrganizing the attacks\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThreat actors are actively spreading malware through Meta’s sponsored ad system.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe malicious campaigns begin with cybercriminals taking over an existing Facebook account. Once compromised, the crooks begin to change descriptions and cover and profile photos, making the page seem as if it is run by well-known AI-based image and video generators.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe cybercriminals then begin boosting the legitimacy of the page with news, AI-generated photos and advertisements that contain descriptions of enhancements of the impersonated AI service and links that give users free access or trials for the tool.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe point of the malicious campaign is to trick individuals into accessing a malicious link and downloading malware onto devices.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAlthough many of the malicious ads inspected by Bitdefender researchers urged individuals to download the purported new version of the AI tool from Dropbox and Google Drive links – which is undoubtedly a huge red flag – the campaign impersonating Midjourney used a different approach.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ECybercriminals created over a dozen malicious websites mimicking the official Midjourney landing page to lure users into downloading the latest version of the service via a GoFile link.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"threat-actors-serve-a-four-course-menu-of-info-stealers\"\u003EThreat actors serve a four-course menu of info stealers\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ECybercriminals have created a highly engaging distribution system for malicious software through the Malware-as-a-service (MaaS) business model that enables any malicious individual to conduct sophisticated and cost-efficient attacks and other nefarious activities.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis includes stealing sensitive information, compromising online accounts, committing fraud, disrupting operations, or demanding ransom after encrypting data on a compromised system.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe malvertising campaigns analyzed by our researchers have been distributing an assortment of malicious software that poses severe risks to consumers’ devices, data and identity. Users who’ve interacted with the malware-serving ads could have unknowingly downloaded and deployed harmful files onto their devices: Rilide Stealer, Vidar Stealer, IceRAT (written in JPHP) and Nova Stealer.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"rilide-stealer-v4\"\u003ERilide Stealer V4\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EResearchers at Bitdefender Labs have spotted an updated version of the Rilide Stealer (V4) in various sponsored ad campaigns impersonating AI-based software or photo editors including Sora, CapCut, Gemini AI, Photo Effects Pro and CapCut Pro.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe malware known as Rilide is a malicious extension that targets Chromium-based browsers, including Google Chrome, Opera, Brave and Microsoft Edge, and enables threat actors to monitor browsing history, capture login credentials, and even withdraw crypto funds by bypassing 2FA through script injections.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EWhat’s new for Rilide V4:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe malicious extension mainly targets Facebook cookies\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EIt masquerades as a Google Translate Extension\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe threat actor uses better obfuscation techniques to hide the true intent of the software. The so-called app installer for the AI software immediately opens the official webpage of the impersonated AI image generator to fool users. At the same time, it begins loading the malicious extension onto the victim’s browsers.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EIndicators of Highly focused on enhancing their deceptive practices, threat actors have, unfortunately, found a most reliable and powerful a","\u002Fblog\u002Flabs\u002Fai-meets-next-gen-info-stealers-in-social-media-malvertising-campaigns\u002F","66d5c3d2d0ec1aefc7d722cf","Notes on ThroughTek Kalay Vulnerabilities and Their Impact on the IoT Ecosystem","notes-on-throughtek-kalay-vulnerabilities-and-their-impact","https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F05\u002Fcomputer-8037837_1920.jpg","2024-05-15T16:00:00.000+03:00","\u003Cp\u003ESince 2014, Bitdefender IoT researchers have been looking into the world's most popular IoT devices, hunting for vulnerabilities and undocumented attack avenues. This report documents four vulnerabilities affecting devices powered by the ThroughTek Kalay Platform. Due to the platform’s massive presence in IoT integrations, these flaws have a significant downstream impact on several vendors.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn the interconnected landscape of the Internet of Things (IoT), the reliability and security of devices, infrastructure and data are paramount. Among the many frameworks facilitating the operation of IoT devices, ThroughTek's Kalay platform stands as a linchpin, powering \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.throughtek.com\u002Fadvantages\u002F?ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003Emore than 100 million devices worldwide\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. With a predominant presence in surveillance cameras and security devices, ThroughTek Kalay's influence underscores its significance in safeguarding homes, businesses, and integrators alike.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003ENOTE: the vulnerabilities presented in this paper have been responsibly disclosed to the affected vendors. Specific firmware information is available in each report below. We would like to extend our thanks to the involved vendors for their prompt acknowledgement of vulnerability and rapid patch release.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"timeline\"\u003E\u003Cem\u003ETimeline\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EOct 19, 2023: Bitdefender contacts ThroghTek and sends the vulnerability report.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EOct 20, 2023: Vendor confirms the issues.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EOct 26, 2023: Vendor asks for over 90-day time extension to implement and deploy the fix.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMar 15, 2024: Additional extension is requested.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EApr 12, 2024: Coordinated vulnerability disclosure is scheduled for May 15 2024 to allow all affected parties to apply the patches\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EApr 16, 2024: Vendor confirms that all affected SDK versions have been patched.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMay 15, 2024: This report becomes public.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"vulnerabilities-exposed\"\u003EVulnerabilities Exposed\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6321&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6321\u003C\u002Fa\u003E allows an authenticated user to run system commands as the root user leading to the full compromise of the device.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6322&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6322\u003C\u002Fa\u003E  enables attackers to gain root access through a stack-based buffer overflow vulnerability in the handler of an IOCTL message, typically employed in configuring motion detection zones in cameras. This is a vulnerability specific to some devices that use motion detection features.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6323&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6323\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, for instance, exposes a loophole wherein a local attacker can illicitly obtain the AuthKey secret, effectively helping an attacker establish a preliminary connection to the victim device.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ELastly, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6324&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6324 \u003C\u002Fa\u003Eexploits a vulnerability allowing attackers to infer the pre-shared key for a DTLS session, a critical prerequisite for connecting and talking to the victim devices.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhen chained together, these vulnerabilities facilitate unauthorized root access from within the local network, as well as remote* code execution to completely subvert the victim device.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E*Remote code execution is only possible after the device has been probed from the local network.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"affected-vendors\"\u003EAffected vendors\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhile these vulnerabilities affect the TUTK platform and subsequently impact most implementations, our research was conducted on three major devices sold worldwide. Given that some vendors had device-specific vulnerabilities, individual timelines are available in each report.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"owlet-cam-v1-and-v2\"\u003EOwlet Cam v1 and v2\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EOwlet Cam uses the ThroughTek Kalay solution to communicate with clients over the Internet.  The three vulnerabilities (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6323&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6323\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6324&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6324\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6321&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6321\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) can be chained together to allow an attacker to obtain root access from the local network and then to execute commands on the device. On Owlet Cam, command execution is obtained via \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6321&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6321\u003C\u002Fa\u003E - a vulnerability in IOCTL message 0x6008E, which is used to unpack archives containing OTA updates.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EA technical dive into the vulnerabilities and how they are daisy-chained to compromise the Owlet Cam is available below:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-begin: html--\u003E\u003Cp align=\"center\"\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Ffiles\u002F2024\u002F05\u002FBitdefender-PReport-owlet-7745.pdf\" class=\"button-view-all d-inline-block\"\u003EDownload the whitepaper\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-end: html--\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"wyze-cam-v3\"\u003EWyze Cam v3\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBitdefender researchers have identified three vulnerabilities in Wyze Cam v3. They are tracked as CVE-\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6322&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003E2023-6322\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6323&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6323\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6324&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6324\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Chained together, these vulnerabilities allow an attacker to obtain root access from the local network. In this case, command execution on the Wyze Cam v3 is obtained via \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6322&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6322\u003C\u002Fa\u003E - a stack-based buffer overflow vulnerability in the handler of IOCTL message 0x284C that is used to set the motion detection zone.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EA technical dive into the vulnerabilities and how they are daisy-chained to compromise the Wyze Cam v3 is available below:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-begin: html--\u003E\u003Cp align=\"center\"\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Ffiles\u002F2024\u002F05\u002FBitdefender-PReport-Wyze-7745.pdf\" class=\"button-view-all d-inline-block\"\u003EDownload the whitepaper\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-end: html--\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"roku-indoor-camera-se\"\u003ERoku Indoor Camera SE\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe vulnerabilities in the Roku Indoor Camera SE are identical to those in Wyze Cam v3 (and potentially other security cameras). Bitdefender researchers have daisy-chained CVE-\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6322&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003E2023-6322\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6323&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6323\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6324&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6324\u003C\u002Fa\u003Eto obtain the necessary prerequisites for talking to the camera and for running OS commands as root user.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EA technical dive into the vulnerabilities and how they are daisy-chained to compromise the Roku Indoor Camera SE is available below:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-begin: html--\u003E\u003Cp align=\"center\"\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Ffiles\u002F2024\u002F05\u002FBitdefender-PReport-roku-7745.pdf\" class=\"button-view-all d-inline-block\"\u003EDownload the whitepaper\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-end: html--\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"implications-and-remediation\"\u003EImplications and Remediation:\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe ramifications of these vulnerabilities extend far beyond the realm of theoretical exploits, as they directly impact on the privacy and safety of users relying on devices powered by ThroughTek Kalay. Our findings have been responsibly disclosed both to the platform vendor, as well as to the tested integrators. Updated versions of firmware and SDKs have been made available for the impacted devices to prevent these issues from being exploited in real-life scenarios.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E","Since 2014, Bitdefender IoT researchers have been looking into the world's most popular IoT devices, hunting for vulnerabilities and undocumented attack avenues. This report documents four vulnerabilities affecting devices powered by the ThroughTek Kalay Platform. Due to the platform’s massive presence in IoT integrations, these flaws have a significant downstream impact on several vendors.\n\nIn the interconnected landscape of the Internet of Things (IoT), the reliability and security of devices,",3,"\u002Fblog\u002Flabs\u002Fnotes-on-throughtek-kalay-vulnerabilities-and-their-impact\u002F","66d5c3d2d0ec1aefc7d722ce","Vulnerabilities Identified in LG WebOS","vulnerabilities-identified-in-lg-webos","https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002Fweb-4869856_1920.jpg","2024-04-09T16:00:00.000+03:00","\u003Cp\u003EAs the creator of the world’s first smart home cybersecurity hub, Bitdefender regularly audits popular IoT hardware for vulnerabilities. This research paper is part of a broader program that aims to shed light on the security of the world’s best-sellers in the IoT space. This report covers vulnerabilities discovered while researching the LG WebOS TV operating system.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe have found several issues affecting WebOS versions 4 through 7 running on LG TVs. These vulnerabilities let us gain root access on the TV after bypassing the authorization mechanism. Although the vulnerable service is intended for LAN access only, Shodan, the search engine for Internet-connected devices, identified over 91,000 devices that \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.shodan.io\u002Fsearch?query=product%3A%22LG+webOs+TV%22&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003Eexpose this service to the Internet\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002Fimage-1.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"392\" height=\"206\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"vulnerabilities-at-a-glance\"\u003EVulnerabilities at a glance\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EBitdefender researchers discovered a vulnerability that lets an attacker bypass the authorization mechanism in WebOS versions 4 through 7. By setting a variable, the attacker can add an extra user to the TV set (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6317&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6317)\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EAnother vulnerability allows attackers to elevate the access they gained in the first step to root and fully take over the device (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6318&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6318\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EA third vulnerability (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6319&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6319\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) allows operating system command injection by manipulating a library responsible with showing music lyrics.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6320&ref=blogapp.bitdefender.com\"\u003ECVE-2023-6320\u003C\u002Fa\u003E vulnerability lets an attacker inject authenticated commands by manipulating the \u003Ccode\u003Ecom.webos.service.connectionmanager\u002Ftv\u002FsetVlanStaticAddress\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003EAPI endpoint.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"vulnerable-os-versions\"\u003EVulnerable OS versions\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EwebOS 4.9.7 - 5.30.40 running on LG43UM7000PLA\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EwebOS 5.5.0 - 04.50.51 running on OLED55CXPUA\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EwebOS 6.3.3-442 (kisscurl-kinglake) - 03.36.50 running on OLED48C1PUB\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EwebOS 7.3.1-43 (mullet-mebin) - 03.33.85 running on OLED55A23LA\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"disclosure-timeline\"\u003EDisclosure timeline\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003ENovember 01, 2023: Vendor disclosure\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ENovember 15, 2023: Vendor confirms the vulnerabilities.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EDecember 14, 2023: Vendor requests extension\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMarch 22, 2024: Patch release\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EApril 09, 2024: Public release of this report\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"a-technical-look-into-the-discovered-vulnerabilities\"\u003EA technical look into the discovered vulnerabilities\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWebOS runs a service on ports 3000\u002F3001 (HTTP\u002FHTTPS\u002FWSS) which is used by the LG ThinkQ smartphone app to control the TV. To set up the app, the user must enter a PIN code into the display on the TV screen. An error in the account handler lets an attacker skip the PIN verification entirely and create a privileged user profile.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-1.jpg\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"880\" height=\"660\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-1.jpg 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-1.jpg 880w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe function that handles account registration requests uses a variable called \u003Cstrong\u003EskipPrompt\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E which is set to true when either the \u003Ccode\u003Eclient-key\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E or the \u003Ccode\u003Ecompanion-client-key\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E parameters correspond to an existing profile. It also takes into consideration what permissions are requested when deciding whether to prompt the user for a PIN, as confirmation is not required in some cases.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe can request the creation of an account with no permissions, which will be automatically granted. Then we request another account with elevated permissions, but we specify the \u003Ccode\u003Ecompanion-client-key\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Evariable to match the key we got when we created the first account. The server will confirm that this key exists but will not verify if it belongs to the correct account. Thus, the \u003Cstrong\u003EskipPrompt\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E variable will be true and the account will be created without requesting a PIN confirmation on the TV.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis vulnerability, identified as CVE-2023-6317, has been confirmed to affect webOS 4.9.7, 5.5.0, 6.3.3-442, and 7.3.1-43.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHaving created a privileged account without user interaction, we now have access to a large attack surface that was inaccessible before. We have found two authenticated command injection vulnerabilities that lead to root access, and another that runs commands as the dbus user.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"authenticated-command-injection-in-the-processanalyticsreport-method-from-the-comwebosservicecloudupload-service\"\u003EAuthenticated command injection in the processAnalyticsReport method from the com.webos.service.cloudupload service\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe \u003Ccode\u003EprocessAnalyticsReport\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E method requires three parameters: \u003Ccode\u003Etype\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, \u003Ccode\u003EreportFile\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, and \u003Ccode\u003EoriginalFile\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. When the \u003Ccode\u003Etype\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eparameter is set to \u003Ccode\u003Eanalytic\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E the \u003Ccode\u003EreportFile\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eparameter will be passed to a system command without being sanitized.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAlthough requests to this method cannot be performed directly, we can use another endpoint, \u003Cem\u003Esystem.notifications\u002FcreateAlert\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, to bypass this restriction, accessible only to authenticated users who have the \u003Ccode\u003EWRITE_NOTIFICATION_TOAST\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E permission. The \u003Cem\u003Eonclose \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eparameter supported by this endpoint allows us to perform internal requests to services that are not exposed, similar to SSRF. After we create the notification, we trigger the \u003Cem\u003Eonclose \u003C\u002Fem\u003Ecall through the \u003Ccode\u003Esystem.notifications\u002FcloseAlert\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E endpoint, performing the request to the vulnerable endpoint.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe specified file must exist on the device, but we can bypass this constraint by using the \u003Cem\u003Edownload \u003C\u002Fem\u003Emethod from the \u003Cstrong\u003Ecom.webos.service.downloadmanager \u003C\u002Fstrong\u003Eservice, which will create a file in the \u003Ccode\u003E\u002Fmedia\u002Finternal\u002Fdownloads\u002F\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E directory with an arbitrary filename. Both the \u003Ccode\u003EprocessAnalyticsReport\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eand download\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Emethods can be accessed through the \u003Ccode\u003EcreateAlert\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eendpoint.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe vulnerable command is created on line 83 and executed on line 84:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-2.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"526\" height=\"198\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis vulnerability, identified as CVE-2023-6318, has been confirmed to affect webOS 5.5.0, 6.3.3-442, and 7.3.1-43.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"authenticated-command-injection-in-the-getaudiometadata-method-from-the-comwebosserviceattachedstoragemanager-service\"\u003EAuthenticated command injection in the getAudioMetadata method from the com.webos.service.attachedstoragemanager service\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe \u003Cem\u003EgetAudioMetadata \u003C\u002Fem\u003Emethod requires two parameters: \u003Ccode\u003EdeviceId\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and \u003Ccode\u003EfullPath\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. While the \u003Cem\u003EdeviceId \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eparameter is not important, the \u003Cem\u003EfullPath \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eparameter will be passed, under certain conditions, to a system command without being sanitized. If this parameter points to a file with the \u003Cem\u003E.mp3\u003C\u002Fem\u003E extension the service will search in the same directory for the corresponding lyrics file with the same name (\u003Cem\u003E.lrc\u003C\u002Fem\u003E extension). If found, the first four bytes of the lyrics file will be compared with the sequence \u003Ccode\u003E\\xFF\\xFE\\x00\\x00\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. If they match (meaning that the file is UTF1632 encoded) the service will try to decode it using the \u003Cem\u003Eiconv\u003C\u002Fem\u003E binary. This binary will be called together with the full filename without prior sanitization, leading to command injection.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBoth the .mp3 and .lrc files must exist on the device and can be created using the \u003Ccode\u003Edownload\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Emethod mentioned earlier. All required methods can be accessed through the \u003Ccode\u003EcreateAlert\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E endpoint.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe vulnerable code in \u003Cem\u003EconvLrcStringByBinary \u003C\u002Fem\u003Efrom the \u003Cem\u003Easm \u003C\u002Fem\u003Ebinary:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-3.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"550\" height=\"36\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis vulnerability, identified as CVE-2023-6319, has been confirmed to affect webOS 4.9.7, 5.5.0, 6.3.3-442, and 7.3.1-43.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"authenticated-command-injection-in-the-comwebosserviceconnectionmanagertvsetvlanstaticaddress-endpoint-allows-execution-of-commands-on-the-device-as-dbus\"\u003EAuthenticated command injection in the com.webos.service.connectionmanager\u002Ftv\u002FsetVlanStaticAddress endpoint allows execution of commands on the device as dbus\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe \u003Ccode\u003EsetVlanStaticAddress\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eendpoint requires three parameters: \u003Ccode\u003Eip_address\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, \u003Ccode\u003Ebcast_address\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, and \u003Ccode\u003Enetmask\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. All threeparameters will be passed to a system command without being sanitized. Before calling this endpoint, we must first call the \u003Ccode\u003EcreateVirtualLan\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eendpoint.
